SEMESTER S5 
CRYPTOGRAPHY FOR CPS 
Course Code 
PECPT523 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PECPT 413 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamental concepts of Classical and modern Cryptosystem. 
2. To compare various private and public key Cryptosystem for encryption, key exchange and 
authentication algorithms. 
3. To understand the different applications of cryptography. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Integer Arithmetic - Divisibility - Greatest Common Divisor - Extended 
Euclidean Algorithm- Linear Diophantine equation,  
Modular Arithmetic - Modulo Operator - Congruence - Addition and 
multiplicative inverse, Algebraic structures - Field – Finite fields of the form 
GF(p) and GF(2n) - Polynomial arithmetic,  
Prime Numbers – Fermat’s and Euler’s Theorem - Prime Factorization by Trial 
Division Method - Chinese Remainder Theorem.   
Security Goals - Security Services - Confidentiality -Integrity - Authentication- 
Nonrepudiation- Access control,  
Security Mechanisms – Encipherment- Data Integrity – Signature - 
Authentication Exchange - Traffic Padding- Routing Control – Notarization 
Access Control 
9 

 
 
2 
Introduction to Cryptography -Classification of Cryptosystems - Cryptanalytic 
attacks - CipherProperties – Confusion - Diffusion. 
Classical Cryptosystems - Substitution Techniques - Monoalphabetic Cipher – 
Caesar Cipher- AffineCipher,  
Polyalphabetic Ciphers - Autokey Cipher- Playfair Cipher-Hill 
Cipher-VigenereCipher- One Time Pad Cipher, Stream and Block Ciphers, 
Modern Secret Key Ciphers - Substitution Box-Permutation Box-Product Ciphers 
Data Encryption Standard - DES - Structure of DES - DES Attacks - 2-DES - 3-
DES, 
Advanced Encryption Standard - AES - Structure-Analysis, Cryptographic Hash 
Functions - Properties - Secure Hash Algorithm - SHA-512 Logic - SHA-512 
Round Function, 
Message Authentication Code-Hash-based Message Authentication Code -
HMAC -Cipher-based Message Authentication Code - CMAC 
9 
3 
Public Key Cryptosystems -PKC - Types of PKC - Trapdoor - One-way 
functions, RSA Cryptosystem -Key Generation – Encryption- Decryption, 
ElGamal Cryptosystem – Key Generation – Encryption-Decryption, Diffie-
Hellman Key Exchange Protocol- Man in the Middle attack on Diffie-Hellman 
Protocol. 
Digital Signature- Signing - Verification, Digital signature forgery-Existential 
forgery- Selective forgery - Universal forgery, RSA Digital Signature Scheme -
ElGamal Signature Scheme. 
9 
4 
Symmetric Key Distribution using Symmetric and Asymmetric Encryption - 
Distribution of public keys -Public announcement- Public available directory-
Public-key authority- Public key Certificates. 
Electronic Mail Security -Pretty Good Privacy- PGP message format - 
Transmission and Reception of PGP Messages, IP Security Overview - IP 
Authentication Header - Encapsulating Security Payload - Distributed Denial of 
Service attacks, Secure Electronic Transaction – Payment Processing - Dual 
Signature,  
Firewalls - Firewall Design Principles 
9

SEMESTER S5 
INTERFACE DESIGN FOR CPS 
Course Code 
PECPT524 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PECPT 414 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand various types of input and output devices used in CPS, including sensors, 
actuators, displays, and feedback mechanisms, and their integration into system designs. 
2. To understand the challenges and considerations involved in integrating input and output 
devices into CPS architectures, ensuring seamless operation and effective user interaction. 
3. To illustrate methods for evaluating CPS interfaces, including usability testing, validation 
techniques, and assessing interface effectiveness in real-world scenarios. 
4. To explore emerging technologies and future trends in CPS interface design, preparing 
students to adapt to advancements in the field. 
 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1

Introduction to Interface Design - Overview of interface design principles, 
Importance of interfaces in Cyber-Physical Systems

relevance to CPS, Cognitive psychology principles in interface design 
User-centered Design Process - Understanding user needs and requirements, 
Methods for gathering and analyzing user data in CPS contexts, Interface 
Design Methodologies - Design thinking and iterative design processes, 
Prototyping techniques for CPS interfaces 
9

interfaces: 
technologies,

integrating input devices into CPS architectures, Data acquisition, processing, 
and communication protocols 
9

for real-time data in CPS

CPS environments, Ensuring accessibility for diverse user groups in CPS 
interface design

coordination of output devices with system responses

world scenarios, Validation techniques for ensuring interface reliability and 
performance

impact on CPS interface design, Predictions and discussions on the future 
directions of CPS interfaces

Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To identify the significance of implementing virtualization techniques. 
2. To interpret the various cloud computing models and services 
3. To compare the various public cloud platforms and software environments.  
4. To apply appropriate cloud programming methods to solve big data problems. appreciate the 
need of security mechanisms in cloud 
5. To illustrate the use of various cloud services available online. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours

aService(PaaS),Software-as-a-Service

(Anything-as-a-

Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
Students should evaluate and analyze a real-world problem, assess the proposed solutions, conclude 
which solution is most appropriate for the problem, and then implement the chosen solution using 
executable code or simulate it using relevant software or supported hardware platforms. 
 

 
 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the real-world problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, 
objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with evidence and logical 
reasoning. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compares trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Considers feasibility, scalability, and practical implications. 
4. Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions. 
b. Successfully translates the chosen solution into an executable code or 
simulation using relevant software suit or supported hardware platform. 
c. Demonstrates proficiency in simulation / emulation practices (readability, 
efficiency, error handling). 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S5 
DSP LAB 
Course Code 
PCCPL507 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
0: 0: 3: 0 
ESE Marks 
50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCCPT402 
Course Type 
Practical 
 
Course Objectives:  
1. To create discrete time signals and test the sampling theorem. 
2. To Formulate the DFT for a discrete signal and verification of its properties using Python/ 
Scilab/MATLAB.  
3. To design and implement algorithms for solving difference equations, computing convolution 
and correlation and verifying their properties using numerical methods and simulations.  
4. To design and test the filtering operations and compare with the theoretical values. 
5. To implement the DSP computations on DSP hardware and verify the result 
Details of Experiment 
(Perform at least 10 Experiments from the list below, in which a minimum of 3 experiments with  
DSP kits are included.) 
Expt. No
Experiment 
1 
Simulation of Signals: Simulate the following signals using Python/ Scilab/MATLAB.  
1. Unit impulse signal 2. Unit pulse signal 3. Unit ramp signal 4. Bipolar pulse  
5. Triangular signal 
2 
Verification of sampling theorem (use interpolation function) using Python/Scilab/MATLAB. 
3 
Verify the properties of DFT (like Linearity and Parseval 's theorem, etc.) using Python/ 
Scilab/MATLAB. 
4 
Compute the DFT of square pulse and Sinc function using Python/ Scilab/MATLAB. 
5 
Find the DFT / IDFT of a given DT signal using Python/ Scilab/MATLAB. 
6 
Find Linear convolution using DFT(Overlap-add and Overlap-Save methods) in Python/ 
Scilab/ MATLAB. 
7 
Find Auto and cross correlation of two sequences and verification of their properties using 
Python/ Scilab/MATLAB. 

 
 
8 
Compute the N point DFT of a given sequence and plot magnitude and phase spectrum (using 
DFT equation and verify it by built-in routine) using Python/ Scilab/MATLAB. 
9 
Design and implement a Lowpass and High pass FIR filter to meet the desired specifications 
(using different window techniques) and test the filter with an audio file. Plot the spectrum of 
audio signal before and after filtering using Python/ Scilab/MATLAB. 
10 
Design and implement a digital IIR filter (Low pass and High pass) to meet given 
specifications and test with an audio file. Plot the spectrum of audio signal before and after 
filtering using Python/ Scilab/MATLAB. 
11 
Obtain the Linear convolution of two sequences using DSP kit 
12 
Obtain the Circular convolution of two sequences using DSP kit 
13 
Compute the N-point DFT of a given sequence using DSP kit 
14 
Determine the Impulse response of first order and second order system using DSP kit 
15 
Generate a sine wave and standard test signals using DSP kit 
16 
Sample an analog signal and study the aliasing effect using DSP kit

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
● Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test understanding 
of the upcoming experiment. 
● Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of 
the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
● Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
● Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
● Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
● Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper documentation 
of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
● Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
 

 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
● Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles 
during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, 
and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
● Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
● Preliminary 
Work 
and 
Planning: 
Thoroughness 
in 
planning 
and 
organizing 
materials/equipment. 
● Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
● Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
● Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or 
programming task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
● Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
● Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
● Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
● Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the subject. 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
● Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

or Gazebo tools.

SEMESTER S6 
SPECIAL PURPOSE MACHINES FOR AUTOMATION 
Course Code 
PCCPT601 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week (L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the basic principles of special purpose machines (SPMs) in automation. 
2. To explore the design, operation, and control of various SPMs. 
3. To gain knowledge about the integration of SPMs into automated systems. 
4. To study the advancements and emerging trends in SPM technology and to solve industrial 
problems 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to Special Purpose Machines: Overview of Special Purpose 
Machines-Definition, scope, and role in automation. Types of Special 
Purpose Machines-Classification based on applications (e.g., assembly 
machines, inspection machines, testing machines). Components and 
Subsystems- Mechanical, electrical, and control components. Comparison 
with General-Purpose Machines-Advantages and limitations. 
11 
2 
Design Principles for Special Purpose Machines: Mechanical Design 
Considerations-Structural design, kinematics, and dynamics. Control 
Systems-PLCs, sensors, actuators, and feedback systems. Integration of 
Components- Combining mechanical and electrical systems for automation. 
Design Methodologies-Approaches to designing efficient and reliable SPMs. 
11 

 
3 
Automation 
Technologies 
and 
Implementation: 
Automation 
Technologies-Overview of technologies used in SPMs (e.g., robotics, vision 
systems, AI). Programming and Control- Writing and implementing control 
algorithms, interfacing with PLCs. Safety and Standards - Safety 
considerations 
and 
industry 
standards 
for 
automation 
systems. 
Troubleshooting Techniques- Common issues and solutions 
11 
4 
Theoretical Aspects of Troubleshooting and Future Trends: Theoretical 
Troubleshooting Techniques-Concepts and strategies for diagnosing and 
resolving issues. Simulation and Testing Theories-Theoretical understanding 
of simulation tools and methodologies. Future Trends and Developments - 
Emerging technologies and future directions in SPMs and automation. 
11

     SEMESTER S6 
             COMMUNICATION FOR CPS 
 
Course Code 
PCCPT602 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCCPT502 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To design and develop communication systems for CPS applications. 
2. To evaluate and optimize CPS communication systems. 
3. To implement secure and efficient communication protocols. 
4. To apply CPS communication technologies to various domains and applications. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to communication for CPS: Overview of CPS and 
communication requirements, Types of communication in CPS (eg: sensor-
sensor, sensor-actuator, actuator-actuator), Communication protocols and 
standards for CPS. Network topologies and architecture for CPS (TCP/IP, 
UDP, HTTP), Network performance matrices (eg: Throughput, latency, 
jitter) 
9 
2 
Wireless communication for CPS: Wireless communication technologies 
(Wi-Fi, Bluetooth, Zigbee) Wireless network protocols and standards 
(802.11,802.15.4), Wireless Communication challenges (interference, 
fading), Wired communication for CPS: Wired communication technologies 
(Ethernet, USB, CAN), Wired network topologies and standards (TCP/IP, 
UDP, Modbus) 
9 

 
3 
Data compression and Encryption for CPS: Data compression techniques 
(Huffman coding, LZ77), Encryption techniques (AES, ESA), Data 
compression and Encryption algorithms for CPS) 
Communication protocols for CPS applications: IoT communication 
protocols (MQTT, CoAP, LWM2M), Industrial automatic communication 
protocols (Modbus, Profibus, Profinet), Healthcare communication 
protocols (HL7, DICOM) 
9 
4 
Performance Evaluation and Optimization: Performance matrices for 
CPS 
communication 
(throughput, 
latency, 
reliability) 
performance 
Evaluation tools (simulation, testing), Optimization techniques for CPS 
communication (buffer sizing, packet scheduling), Security and Privacy in 
CPS communication: Threats and vulnerabilities in CPS communication, 
Security measures for CPS communication (encryption and authentication), 
privacy concerns and solutions in CPS communication. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
ADVANCED MICROCONTROLLERS 
 
Course Code 
PECPT631 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCCPT302 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand RISC and ARM Design Philosophy 
2. To gain in-depth knowledge of the ARM core data flow model. 
3. To explore THUMB and ARM Programming 
4. To provide a detailed understanding of exception handling in ARM processors 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
ARM Embedded Systems and ARM Processor Fundamentals: The RISC 
design philosophy, ARM design philosophy, embedded system hardware- 
AMBA bus protocol, embedded system software- applications. ARM core 
data flow model, Registers, CPSR-Processor modes, Banked registers. 
Pipeline- Characteristics. 
9 
2 
ARM Instruction Set: Fundamentals of ARM instructions, Barrel shifter, 
Classification and explanation of instructions with examples-Data 
processing, Branch, Load-store, SWI and Program Status Register 
instruction. 
9 
3 
Introduction to THUMB and ARM Programming: Introduction to 
THUMB, Differences between ARM and THUMB, Register usage in 
Thumb, ARM Thumb Interworking. General Structure of ARM assembly 
module, Assembler directives- AREA, ENTRY, END, SPACE, DCD, DCB, 
DCW, DCI, DCQ, EQU, EXPORT, ALIGN, CODE16, CODE32, DATA. 
Simple ALP programs on Arithmetic & logical operations, Factorial, string 
operation, sorting, searching, and Scan 
9 

 
4 
Exception and Interrupt handling schemes: Exception handling- ARM 
processor exceptions and modes, vector table, exception priorities, link 
register offsets. Interrupts- assigning interrupts, interrupt latency, IRQ and 
FIQ exceptions with example- code for enabling and disabling IRQ and FIQ 
exceptions, Comparison between exception and interrupts. Interrupt handling 
schemes- nested interrupt handler, non-nested interrupt handler. Basic 
interrupt stack design. 
9

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the principles of networked control systems and their advantages over 
traditional control systems. 
2. To study the impact of network-induced delays and packet losses on control system 
performance. 
3. To analyze different control strategies to mitigate the adverse effects of network issues. 
4. To design and implement networked control systems for real-world applications. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Networked Control Systems: Fundamentals of networked 
control systems, Advantages and challenges, Applications of networked 
control systems, Network protocols and communication architectures 
9 
2 
Network-induced Issues: Network delays and their modelling, Packet 
losses and their impact, Sampling and data quantization.  
9 
3 
Control Strategies for Networked Systems: Predictive control. Robust 
control techniques, Event-triggered and self-triggered control, Compensation 
strategies for delays and losses.  
9 
4 
Design and Implementation: System design methodologies, Simulation 
tools and environments, Real-time implementation, Performance analysis 
and optimization.  
9

Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Introduction to overview of network security issues, cryptographic algorithms, authentication 
techniques 
2. To understand various Protocols and Transport Layer Security (TLS). 
3. To study various attacks and threats in systems and  security in new generation systems 
4. To understand various Cyber risk assessment methods 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
 Introduction (overview of network security issues, cryptographic algorithms, 
authentication techniques) - Layer 2/3 security - Authentication systems,

transport and application layers (SSL/TLS, email security, PGP) - 
Vulnerabilities of Internet protocols 
9 
2 
Secure Sockets Layer (SSL) - SSL Protocol Stack - SSL Record Protocol

and limitations - Kerberos Vulnerabilities Transport Layer Security (TLS). 
9 

 
3

prevention - Routing protocols security and router security - Domain name 
server (DNS) security - Traffic monitoring, Intrusion detection, Honeypots - 
Wireless networks security - Spam, Phishing, and Pharming - Malware 
propagation and containment, Botnets - Anonymity and privacy on the Web. 
Internet Security Protocols and Standards - TCP Attacks, DNS 
Vulnerabilities, SSL/TLS, DDoS - Next Generation System Designs and 
Challenges  
Cyber-Physical System Overview and Security - Internet of Things and 
Smart Grid Security - Data & Infrastructure Security in Cloud/Edge 
Computing. 
9 
4 
Blockchain and Decentralized Applications- Hash cash and other Consensus 
Protocols Blockchain Security- Smart Contracts - Scalability and Privacy 
challenges, Security Economics and Risk Modelling - Cyber-Risk 
Assessment - Threat Information Sharing - Cyber-insurance 
9

SEMESTER S6 
MACHINE LEARNING FOR CPS 
 
Course Code 
PECPT635 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBCPT 404 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamental concepts of Machine Learning (ML) and its relevance to 
Cyber-Physical Systems (CPS). 
2. To gain proficiency in implementing supervised, unsupervised, and reinforcement learning 
algorithms. 
3. To explore the real-time applications of ML in optimizing and controlling CPS. 
4. To learn advanced ML techniques and understand the ethical, security, and privacy 
considerations in CPS. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Machine Learning  
Basics of Machine Learning: Definition and significance, Types of 
Machine Learning: Supervised, Unsupervised, Reinforcement Learning, 
Common algorithms and their applications, The role of Machine Learning in 
CPS 
9 
2 
Supervised and Unsupervised Learning for CPS 
Supervised Learning: Classification algorithms - Decision Trees, Support 
Vector Machines, Regression algorithms- Linear Regression, Polynomial 
Regression, Evaluation metrics- accuracy, precision, recall 
Unsupervised Learning: Clustering algorithms (K-means, Hierarchical 
Clustering), Dimensionality reduction techniques (PCA, t-SNE) 
9 

 
3 
Reinforcement Learning and Real-Time Applications in CPS Reinforcement 
Learning (RL): Fundamentals of RL, Key concepts: states, actions, rewards, 
policy, Q-learning and Deep Q-networks 
Real-Time Applications: ML in real-time decision making, Optimization of 
control systems 
9 
4 
Advanced Topics and Future Trends in ML for CPS 
Advanced ML Techniques: Deep Learning and Neural Networks, Transfer 
Learning, Explainable AI 
Future Trends and Challenges: Edge Computing and IoT integration, 
Security and privacy concerns in CPS, Ethical considerations in ML 
applications 
9 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
Students should evaluate and analyze a real-world problem, assess the proposed solutions, 
conclude which solution is most appropriate for the problem, and then implement the chosen 
solution using executable code or simulate it using relevant software or supported hardware 
platforms. 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the real-world problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, 
objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with evidence and logical 
reasoning. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compares trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Considers feasibility, scalability, and practical implications. 

 
4. Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions. 
b. Successfully translates the chosen solution into an executable code or 
simulation using relevant software suit or supported hardware platform. 
c. Demonstrates proficiency in simulation / emulation practices (readability, 
efficiency, error handling). 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed. 
 
End Semester Examination Marks (ESE): 
 
In Part A, all questions need to be answered and in Part B, each student can choose 
any one full question out of two questions

PCCPT303 
Course Type 
PC-PBL 
Course Objectives: 
1.  To understand and apply advanced control strategies for CPS. 
2.  To analyze and implement security measures specific to CPS environments. 
3.  To evaluate real-time systems within the context of CPS. 
4.  To investigate and propose solutions for complex CPS challenges in various domains. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Advanced Control Strategies:  
Nonlinear Control Systems - Introduction to nonlinear dynamics and 
control, Lyapunov methods and stability analysis. 
Optimal and Robust Control - Overview of optimal control theory, 
Robust control techniques and their applications. 
Adaptive and Learning-Based Control - Adaptive control mechanisms, 
Reinforcement learning in CPS. 
9 
2 
CPS Security and Privacy 
Security Challenges in CPS - Common vulnerabilities and attack 
vectors, Security protocols and encryption techniques. 
Privacy in CPS - Privacy concerns and regulations, Privacy-preserving 
techniques in data collection and processing. 
Intrusion Detection and Response - Techniques for detecting and 
mitigating attacks, Incident response strategies. 
9 

 
3 
Real-Time Systems and Scheduling 
Fundamentals of Real-Time Systems - Real-time system requirements 
and 
classifications, 
Scheduling 
algorithms: 
Rate 
Monotonic 
Scheduling (RMS), Earliest Deadline First (EDF). 
Real-Time Communication Protocols - Communication protocols in 
real-time 
CPS, 
Network-on-Chip 
(NoC) 
and 
Time-Triggered 
Protocols.

management 
9 
4 
Interdisciplinary Applications of CPS 
CPS in Healthcare - Applications and challenges in healthcare CPS 
CPS in Smart Cities - Smart infrastructure and urban planning. 
Emerging Trends and Research Overview of cutting-edge research in 
CPS, IoT integration, AI and CPS, edge computing. 
9 
 
Project based learning (8 Hrs) 
 The objective of Project based learning to strengthen the understanding of student’s 
fundamentals through effective application of theoretical concepts.  Projects can help to boost 
student’s skills and widen the horizon of their thinking. 
 The ultimate aim of an engineering student is to resolve a problem by applying theoretical 
knowledge. 
 In the beginning, students shall be given an awareness and/or guideline on how to implement 
and learn this course through a project and form groups in the first few weeks. 
 Each group should identify a project that can be done to understand a part of the contents of 
this course and perform a literature survey. 
 Choose a suitable platform for your application and the input output devices to be interfaced. 
 Develop the block diagram and present before the jury within first month after the 
commencement of classes. 
 Implement necessary hardware and software to develop the prototype. 
 Prepare a report and present before the jury for final evaluation.

SEMESTER S6 
IOT AND APPLICATIONS 
Course Code 
OECPT612 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3: 0: 0: 0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
_ 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamentals of IoT, its vision, and strategic research directions. 
2. To explore various connectivity technologies and their application in sensor networks and 
M2M communications 
3. To gain practical experience with Arduino and Raspberry Pi, integrating sensors and 
actuators. 
4. To learn about interoperability in IoT systems and software-defined networking. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to IoT: The Internet of Things Today, Time for Convergence, 
Towards the IoT Universe, Internet of Things Vision, IoT Strategic Research 
and Innovation Directions, IoT Applications, Future Internet Technologies, 
Review of sensing and actuation,  Basics of IoT Networking. 
9 
2 
Connectivity Technologies, Sensor Networks, UAV networks. 
Machine-to-Machine Communications: M2M to IoT – A Basic Perspective– 
Introduction, Some Definitions, M2M Value Chains, IoT Value chains, 
LoRa Technology in M2M Communications:- Introduction to LoRa and 
LoRaWAN, LoRa Protocols and Standards,  Applications of LoRa in M2M 
and IoT 
9 

 
3 
Interoperability in IoT, Introduction to Arduino Programming, Integration of 
Sensors and Actuators with Arduino. 
Introduction to Raspberry Pi, Implementation of IoT with Raspberry Pi, 
Software Defined Networking, Software Defined IoT Networking 
9 
4 
Smart and Connected Cities-An IoT Strategy for Smarter Cities-Vertical IoT 
Needs for Smarter Cities, Global vs. Siloed Strategies-Smart City IoT 
Architecture-Street Layer, City Layer, Data Center Layer, Services Layer- 
Smart City Security Architecture - Smart City Use-Case Examples – Street 
lighting, smart parking, smart traffic and air pollution monitoring 
9

SEMESTER S6 
NETWORKING AND COMMUNICATION PROTOCOLS   
Course Code 
OECPT613 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
_ 
Course Type             Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To introduce the fundamental various types of computer networks. 
2. To demonstrate the TCP/IP and OSI models with merits and demerits. 
3. To explore the various layers of OSI Model. 
4. To introduce UDP and TCP Models. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Network hardware, Network software, OSI, TCP/IP Reference models, 
Example Networks: ARPANET, 
Internet. Physical Layer: Guided Transmission media: twisted pairs, coaxial 
cable, fiber optics, Wireless transmission. Data link layer: Design issues, 
framing, Error detection and correction. 
9 
2 
Elementary data link protocols: 
Simplex protocol, A simplex stop and wait protocol for an error-free 
channel, A simplex stop and wait protocol for noisy channel. Sliding 
Window protocols: A one-bit sliding window protocol, A protocol using Go-
Back-N, A protocol using Selective Repeat, Example data link protocols. 
Medium Access sub layer: The channel allocation problem, Multiple access 
protocols: ALOHA, Carrier sense multiple access protocols, collision free 
protocols. Wireless LANs, Data link layer switching. 
9 

 
3 
Network Layer: Design issues, Routing algorithms: shortest path routing, 
Flooding, Hierarchical routing, Broadcast, Multicast, distance vector routing, 
Congestion Control Algorithms, Quality of Service 
Internetworking, The Network layer in the internet. 
9 
4 
Transport Layer: Transport Services, Elements of Transport protocols, 
Connection management, TCP and UDP protocols. 
Application Layer –Domain name system, SNMP, Electronic Mail; the 
World WEB, HTTP, Streaming audio and video. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
      INTRODUCTION TO HUMAN MACHINE INTERACTION 
 
Course Code 
OECPT614 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L:T:P:R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To identify User Interface (UI) design principles. 
2. To analysis of effective user friendly interfaces 
3. To apply Interactive Design process in real world applications 
4. To understand various design technologies to meet user requirements. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Foundations Of HMI: The Human: History of User Interface Designing, 
I/O channels, Hardware, Software and Operating environments, The 
Psychopathology of everyday Things, Psychology of everyday actions, 
Reasoning and problem solving. The computer: Devices, Memory, 
processing and networks. Interaction: Models, frameworks, Ergonomics, 
styles, elements, interactivity, Paradigms. 
9 
2 
Design & Software Process: Mistakes performed while designing a 
computer system, Human interaction with computers, importance of human 
characteristics human consideration, Human interaction speeds. Interactive 
Design basics, process, scenarios, navigation, Iteration and prototyping. 
HMI in software process: software life cycle, usability engineering, 
Prototyping in practice, design rationale. Design rules: principles, standards, 
guidelines, rules. Recognize the goals, Goal directed design process. 
Evaluation Techniques: Universal Design. 
9 

 
3 
The graphical User Interface: Popularity of graphics, the concept of direct 
manipulation, graphical systems, Characteristics. Web user Interface: 
Interface popularity, characteristics. The merging of graphical Business 
systems and the Web. Principles of user interface design. 
9 
4 
Mobile Ecosystem: Platforms, Application frameworks: Types of Mobile 
Applications: Widgets, Applications, Games, Mobile 
Information 
Architecture, Mobile 2.0, Mobile Design: Elements of Mobile Design, 
Tools. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
ADVANCED CYBER PHYSICAL SYSTEMS LAB 
Course Objectives:  
1.  To introduce basics of cyber-physical system and Industrial revolution 4.0 concepts. 
2.  To develop an exposition of the challenges in implementing a cyber-physical system. 
3.  To analyze the functional behaviour of CPS based on standard modeling formalisms. 
4.  To design CPS requirements based on operating system and hardware architecture 
constraints. 
5.  To understand the concepts involved in Cyber Physical Systems Security. 
 
Details of Experiment 
(Perform at least 10 Experiments from the list below, in which  
 a minimum of 4 experiments from Exp. No. 1-6 and 6 experiments from Exp. No. 7-14 are included) 
Expt. No
Experiment 
1 
Use simulation tools like MATLAB/ Simulink or Gazebo to model and simulate CPS. 
Validate the simulations with real-world data. 
2 
Login to devicehub.net and create a project then create a virtual device. Add the 
corresponding sensor and actuator to the virtual device. 
3 
 Study the MQTT protocol. Examine the components of the protocol. 
4 
Create a connection from an MQTT capable device/software with an MQTT broker then send 
and receive data using it. 
5 
To configuring the gateways and exchange the data to local database using Dream factory. 
6 
To configuring the gateways and upload the data to cloud server using Dream factory or 
Ubidots. 
7 
Assemble a computer controlled planar robot with 2 rotary joints and fixed link lengths. The 
end effector should move in the 2D plane according to the set values of joint angles. 
Course Code 
PCCPL607 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
0:0:3:0 
ESE Marks 
50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCCPL508 
Course Type 
Practical 

 
8 
For the computer controlled 2D planar robot, when the desired destination position (X,Y) is 
given, move the end effector to this point and display the computed values of joint angles. 
Demonstrate importance of singularities. 
9 
Graphically simulate the forward kinematics of the following 3 joint manipulators  
Cartesian robot b) Cylindrical robot c) Spherical robot d) Articulated robot  
10 
Using suitable programming language, find the homogenous transformation matrix for a set 
of sequential joint movements (translation and rotation) if the parameters of joint movements 
are specified with respect to the fixed frame.  
11 
Repeat the above experiment, if the parameters of joint movements are specified relative to 
the moving frames.  
12 
Using a DC motor and suitable measuring instruments, plot the torque versus current, torque 
versus angular velocity and power versus angular velocity.  
13 
Using ultrasonic sensors, stepper/servo motors and infrared sensors, develop a line follower 
robot that will follow a trajectory, avoiding obstacles on its path.  
14 
Using DC servo / stepper motors, implement a pick and place SCARA robot arm in 3D plane.

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test 
understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
 Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and 
understanding of the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record 
and maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 

 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying 
principles during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, 
and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
 Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
 Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or 
programming task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or 
quality of program output. 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
 Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the 
subject. 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

SEMESTER S7 
REAL TIME OPERATING SYSTEMS 
 
Course Code 
PECPT741 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3: 0: 0: 0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
- 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamental concepts and techniques of Operating Systems. 
2. To study fundamental concepts, design principles and hardware considerations 
3. To explore multithreading concepts, processes, threads, and various scheduling structures. 
4. To Gain practical skills in designing and implementing operating system components to 
optimize system performance and reliability. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Operating System: Computer Hardware Organization, 
BIOS and Boot Process, Multithreading concepts, Processes, Threads, 
Scheduling, Structures - Simple Batch, Multi-programmed, Time-shared, 
Personal Computer, Parallel, Distributed Systems, Real-Time Systems, 
System components, Operating System services. 
9 
2 
Basics of Real Time Concepts: Terminology: RTOS concepts and 
definitions, real-time design issues, examples, Hardware Considerations: 
logic states, CPU, memory, I/O, Architectures, RTOS building blocks, Real-
Time Kernel 
9 
3 
Process Management: Concepts, scheduling, IPC, RPC, CPU Scheduling, 
scheduling criteria, scheduling algorithms Threads: Multi-threading models, 
threading issues, thread libraries, synchronization Mutex: creating, deleting, 
prioritizing mutex, mutex internals 
9 

 
 
4 
Inter-process Communication: Messages, Buffers, mailboxes, queues, 
semaphores, deadlock, priority inversion  
Pipes memory management: - Process stack management, run-time buffer 
size, swapping, overlays, block/page management, replacement algorithms, 
real-time garbage collection 
9

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

SEMESTER S7 
DISTRIBUTED SYSTEMS AND MIDDLEWARE 
 
Course Code 
PECPT742 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamental concepts of distributed systems 
2. To learn about various middleware technologies and their applications 
3. To develop the skills to design and implement distributed applications. 
4. To explore case studies and real-world applications of distributed systems. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Distributed Systems: Definition and characteristics, 
Examples and applications, Challenges in distributed systems. 
Communication in Distributed Systems: Interprocess communication: 
Remote Procedure Call (RPC), Remote Method Invocation (RMI), Message-
oriented communication. 
9 
2 
Middleware Technologies: Overview of middleware, Types of middleware 
(e.g., message-oriented, object-oriented, service-oriented), Middleware 
platforms and frameworks. 
Synchronization and Coordination: Logical clocks, Mutual exclusion, 
Election algorithms. 
9 

 
 
3 
Distributed Middleware: Middleware architecture, Types of middleware, 
Case studies (e.g., CORBA, DCOM). 
Fault Tolerance and Reliability: Fault models, Replication techniques, 
Consensus algorithms. 
9 
4 
Distributed File Systems and Databases: Distributed file system design, 
Distributed databases, Consistency models. 
Security in Distributed Systems: Security threats and vulnerabilities, 
Authentication and authorization, Secure communication protocols. 
9

_ 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Introduction to Privacy in CPS 
2. To understand Privacy Preservation Techniques in CPS 
3. To Implement Privacy in CPS 
4. To introduce the Emerging Trends and Future Directions in Privacy for CPS 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Overview of Cyber-Physical Systems (CPS): 
Definition, characteristics ,Components and architecture of CPS 
Importance of privacy in CPS.  
Fundamentals of Privacy: Definition and dimensions of privacy, Privacy 
principles and frameworks, Legal and ethical considerations 
Privacy Threats and Vulnerabilities in CPS: Types of privacy threats in 
CPS, Attack vectors and vulnerabilities 
Case studies of privacy breaches in CPS 
Introduction to Privacy Enhancing Technologies (PETs): Overview of 
PETs, Role of PETs in CPS, Examples of PETs in practice 
9 
2 
Data Anonymization and Masking: Techniques for data anonymization, 
Data masking methods, Balancing privacy and utility 
Encryption and Secure Communication: Fundamentals of encryption, 
Encryption techniques for CPS, Secure communication protocols 
Access Control and Authentication: Access control mechanisms, 
Authentication 
methods 
in 
CPS, 
Role-based 
access 
control 
(RBAC).Differential Privacy: Concept of differential privacy, Techniques 
and algorithms, Applications of differential privacy in CPS 
9 

 
 
3 
Privacy by Design (PbD): Principles of PbD, Implementing PbD in CPS’, 
Case studies of PbD in action 
Privacy Risk Assessment: Identifying privacy risks in CPS, Conducting 
privacy impact assessments (PIAs),Mitigating privacy risks, Privacy 
Policies and Compliance: Developing privacy policies for CPS, 
Compliance with privacy regulations (e.g., GDPR, CCPA),Monitoring 
and enforcement of privacy policies 
Practical Exercises: Hands-on implementation of privacy-preserving 
techniques, Collaborative project work, Presentation and peer review of 
projects 
9 
4 
Advanced Privacy-preserving Technologies : Homomorphic encryption, 
Secure multi-party computation, Blockchain for privacy 
Privacy in Emerging CPS Applications: Internet of Things (IoT),Smart 
cities and infrastructures, Autonomous systems and robotics 
Privacy Challenges and Opportunities: Current challenges in CPS privacy, 
Research directions and opportunities, Future trends in privacy for CPS 
Case Studies and Real-World Applications: Analysis of privacy-
preserving CPS in various industries, Lessons learned from real-world 
implementations, Future outlook and career opportunities in CPS privacy 
9

Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamentals of UX design and its importance in CPS 
2. To apply user research methods to inform UX design decisions 
3. To design intuitive and user-centred interfaces for CPS devices. 
4. To identify security and privacy concerns in CPS UX, design challenges and opportunities. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1

design 
principles, 
Design 
thinking 
approach, 
Human-Computer 
Interaction (HCI) Design: Principles of HCI design, Interaction design 
patterns, Designing interfaces for CPS devices. 
9 
2 
 User Experience (UX) Design Principles: User experience design 
principles: User journey mapping: Wireframing and prototyping. CPS-
specific UX Design Considerations: Designing for IoT devices and sensors, 
UX design for real-time systems, Security and privacy considerations 
9 
3 
Designing for Smart Systems: Designing for smart homes and buildings, 
UX design for industrial automation, Designing for autonomous systems. 
UX Design for Artificial Intelligence (AI) and Machine Learning (ML) 
Systems: UX design considerations for AI and ML systems, Designing for 
transparency and explainability, UX design for AI-powered CPS applications 
9 

 
 
4

Designing for secure user authentication and authorization, UX design for 
secure data transmission and storage. 
User Experience (UX) Design Tools and Software: Overview of UX design 
tools and software, Proficiency in using UX design tools (e.g., Sketch, 
Figma, Adobe XD), Best practices for UX design tool selection and usage.

SEMESTER S7 
DATA VISUALIZATION AND INTERPRETATION 
 
Course Code 
PECPT745 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3: 0: 0: 0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To interpret data plots and understand core data visualization concepts such as correlation, 
linear relationships, and log scales. 
2. To gain the ability to choose appropriate visualization systems for different types of data.  
3. To apply visualization techniques to improve data interpretability 
4. To develop skills to create visualizations that explain complex data science concepts 
effectively 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to data visualization: Introduction of visual perception, visual 
representation of data, Gestalt principles, information overloads, Creating 
visual representations, visualization reference model, visual mapping, visual 
analytics, Design of visualization applications. 
9 
2 
Visualization systems: Classification of visualization systems, Interaction 
and visualization techniques misleading, Visualization of one, two and multi-
dimensional data, text and text documents. 
9 
3 
Interactive visualization: Why interactivity is needed, Handling multiple 
views, Brushing and Linking, D3 instructions and assignments 
Data Interpretability: Causes of misinterpretation, Role of communicative 
visualization in sciences 
9 

 
 
4 
Visualization in data science: methods and examples- Explaining machine 
learning models, Interpretability challenges and solutions, Transparency and 
human-machine trust, Impactful case studies: biology, healthcare, cyber 
security, climate science, social science.  
9 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
Students should evaluate and analyze a real-world problem, assess the proposed solutions, 
conclude which solution is most appropriate for the problem, and then implement the chosen 
solution using executable code or simulate it using relevant software or supported hardware 
platforms. 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the real-world problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, 
objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with evidence and logical 
reasoning. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compares trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Considers feasibility, scalability, and practical implications. 
4. Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions. 
b. Successfully translates the chosen solution into an executable code or 
simulation using relevant software suit or supported hardware platform. 
c. Demonstrates proficiency in simulation / emulation practices (readability, 
efficiency, error handling). 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
 
 

 
 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S7 
FAULT TOLERANCE IN NETWORKED SYSTEMS 
 
Course Code 
PECPT752 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
GBEST204, 
PBCPT404, 
PECPT522
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand fundamental fault tolerance concepts and their relevance in networked 
systems. 
2. To learn and apply redundancy, replication, and recovery techniques. 
3. To develop skills in fault detection, diagnosis, and recovery strategies. 
4. To explore fault tolerance in various modern networked environments. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Fault Tolerance - Definitions and key concepts, Importance in 
networked systems 
Types of Faults and Failures - Crash failures, omission failures, timing 
failures, and Byzantine failures, Impact on system performance and reliability 
Redundancy and Replication Techniques - Hardware vs. software redundancy, 
Data redundancy (RAID levels and their implications), Replication strategies: 
primary-backup, quorum-based 
9 

 
 
2 
Fault Detection Mechanisms - Basic fault detection techniques: heartbeat, 
monitoring, logging, Tools and frameworks for fault detection (basic 
overview) 
Fault Diagnosis and Isolation - Techniques for identifying and isolating faults, 
Practical examples and simplified tools 
Recovery Strategies - Checkpointing and rollback basics,  Simple transaction 
recovery mechanisms 
9 
3 
Distributed Consensus and Coordination - Introduction to consensus 
algorithms: Paxos, Raft, Basic concepts of coordination services: Zookeeper, 
Consul 
Load Balancing and Failover - Principles of load balancing in fault-tolerant 
systems, Simple failover strategies and practical case studies 
Network Fault Tolerance - Basic network redundancy and routing protocols, 
Handling network partitioning and latency issues 
9 
4 
Fault Tolerance in Modern Systems - Fault tolerance in cloud computing and 
microservices, Real-world applications and case studies 
Security Considerations - Impact of security breaches on fault tolerance, 
Designing fault-tolerant systems with basic security considerations 
Emerging Trends and Future Directions - Fault tolerance in IoT and edge 
computing, Current research and future directions 
Project Presentations and Review - Student presentations of fault-tolerant 
system projects, Review of key concepts and course wrap-up 
9

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

SEMESTER S7 
 INTRUSION DETECTION AND PREVENTION  
 
Course Code 
PECPT753 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L:T:P:R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To understand the fundamental concepts, types, and methodologies of intrusion detection 
systems.  
2. 
To analyze various types of network threats and vulnerabilities, assessing their impact on 
security. 
3. 
To evaluate and compare detection techniques for their effectiveness in identifying intrusions. 
4. 
To study and analyze security protocols like SSL/TLS, IPSec, and SSH in securing data in 
transit. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to Network Security: Overview of Network Security, Types 
of Threats and Attacks, Security Policies and Mechanisms, Introduction to 
Intrusion Detection and Prevention Systems, Intrusion Detection Systems 
(IDS):Definition and Purpose of IDS, Types of IDS- Network-based, Host-
based, and Hybrid IDS Architectures, IDS Components and Functionality, 
Signature-based vs. Anomaly-based Detection. 
9 
2 
Intrusion Prevention Systems (IPS):Definition and Purpose of IPS, 
Differences between IDS and IPS,IPS Techniques and Mechanisms, 
Deployment Strategies for IPS, Challenges in IPS Implementation. 
Detection Techniques: Signature Detection Techniques Anomaly Detection 
Techniques, Statistical Methods for Anomaly Detection. 
9 

 
 
3 
Security Information and Event Management (SIEM):Introduction to 
SIEM, Role of SIEM in Intrusion Detection and Prevention, Log 
Management and Analysis, Correlation of Events, Understanding the role of 
SIEM in network security. Incident Response and Management: Incident 
Response Lifecycle, Identification, Containment, Eradication, and Recovery. 
9 
4 
Emerging Trends and Technologies: Cloud Security and IDS/IPS, IoT 
Security Challenges, Machine Learning and AI in Intrusion Detection, 
Blockchain for Security, Future Trends in Network Security, Network 
Security Protocols: SSL/TLS, IPSec, SSH. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
COGNITIVE SYSTEMS AND AI IN CPS   
 
Course Code 
PECPT754 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Program Elective 5 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand Basic Concepts of Artificial Intelligence and Expert Systems. 
2. To provide knowledge on Various Techniques and Tools involved in Artificial Intelligence. 
 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction: History, Definition of AI, Emulation of human cognitive 
process, knowledge search trade off, stored knowledge, semantic nets. An 
abstract view of modelling, elementary knowledge. Computational logic, 
analysis of compound statements using simple logic connectives, predicate 
logic, knowledge organization and manipulation, knowledge acquisition. 
9 
2 
LISP and other programming languages- introduction to LISP, syntax and 
numerical function, LISP and PROLOG distinction, input output and local 
variables, Interaction and recursion, property list and arrays alternative 
languages, formalized symbolic logics- properties of WFRS, non-deductive 
inference methods. Inconsistencies and uncertainties-Truth maintenance 
systems, default reasoning and closed world assumption, Model and 
temporary logic. 
9 

 
 
3 
Matching techniques- Need for matching, matching problem, partial 
matching, Fuzzy matching, RETE matching algorithm. Knowledge 
organization- Indexing and retrieval techniques, integration of knowledge in 
memory organization systems, Perception, communication and Expert 
systems. Overview of Linguistics, Basic passim techniques, Semantic 
analysis and representation structures, natural language generation and 
system. 
9 
4 
Pattern recognition system- understanding speech recognition, Image 
transformation, low level processing, medium and high level processing, 
vision system architecture, Rule based system architecture, knowledge 
acquisition and validation, knowledge system building tools, use of AI and 
ES in manufacturing and design, types of learning- general learning model, 
performance measures, learning automate genetic algorithm, learning by 
induction - LEX, ID3, INDUCE systems. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
 BIG DATA ANALYTICS 
Course Code 
PECPT755 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PECPT415, PECPT635 
Course Type
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamentals of Big Data and its significance. 
2. To explore the relationship between Big Data and related technologies like Cloud 
Computing and IoT. 
3. To learn about data generation, acquisition, and storage mechanisms for Big Data. 
4. To gain hands-on experience with Hadoop and MapReduce for data processing. 
5. To explore traditional and advanced methods for Big Data analysis. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
INTRODUCTION: Dawn of the Big Data Era, Definition and Features of 
Big Data, Big Data Value, The Development of Big Data, Challenges of Big 
Data.  
RELATED TECHNOLOGIES: Cloud Computing - Cloud Computing 
Preliminaries, Relationship Between Cloud Computing and Big Data, IoT - 
IoT Preliminaries, Relationship Between IoT and Big Data, Data Center, 
Hadoop - Hadoop Preliminaries, Relationship between Hadoop and Big Data 
9 
2 
BIG DATA GENERATION AND ACQUISITION: Big Data Generation-
Enterprise Data, IoT Data, Internet Data, Biomedical Data, Data Generation 
from Other Fields, Big Data Acquisition - Data Collection, Data 
Transportation, Data Pre-processing. 
9 
3 
BIG DATA STORAGE: Storage System for Massive Data, Distributed 
Storage System, Storage Mechanism for Big Data - Database Technology, 
Design Factors, Database Programming Model  
HADOOP & MAP REDUCE: Data Storage and Analysis, Comparison with 
Other Systems, A Brief History of Hadoop, Apache Hadoop and the Hadoop 
Ecosystem, A Weather Dataset, Analyzing the Data with Unix Tools, 
9 

 
 
Analyzing the Data with Hadoop(Map and Reduce, Java MapReduce), 
Scaling Out, Hadoop Streaming, Hadoop Pipes. 
4 
BIG DATA ANALYSIS: Traditional Data Analysis, Big Data Analytic 
Methods, Architecture for Big Data Analysis - Real-Time vs. Offline 
Analysis, Analysis at Different Levels, Analysis with Different Complexity, 
Tools for Big Data Mining and Analysis. 
9 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
Students should evaluate and analyze a real-world problem, assess the proposed solutions, 
conclude which solution is most appropriate for the problem, and then implement the chosen 
solution using executable code or simulate it using relevant software or supported hardware 
platforms. 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the real-world problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, 
objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with evidence and logical 
reasoning. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compares trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Considers feasibility, scalability, and practical implications. 
4. Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions. 
b. Successfully translates the chosen solution into an executable code or 
simulation using relevant software suit or supported hardware platform. 
c. Demonstrates proficiency in simulation / emulation practices (readability, 
efficiency, error handling). 
 
 
 

 
 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

Teaching Hours/Week

Prerequisites (if any) 
- 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To be able to develop simple programs for 8051 using assembly language programming 
2. To interface 8051 microcontroller with peripheral devices.    
3. To understand the architecture and design concept of embedded systems 
4. To be able to design embedded systems based on Arduino. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
8051 
microcontroller: 
Difference 
between 
microprocessor 
and 
microcontroller Architecture, 8051 pin diagram; Architecture, I/O Port 
structure, Register organization - special function registers, Memory 
organization, Instruction set, Addressing modes 
Simple Assembly language programs: Arithmetic (Addition, Subtraction, 
Multiplication & Division),Transfer a block of data from one internal 
memory location to another. 
9 
2 
8051 microcontroller Programming and Peripherals. 
Timers/Counters- Serial Communication, Interrupt structure-programming. 
Interfacing of peripherals – LED (ALP and embedded C programming). 
OLED, LCD, ADC, DAC, sensors, simple Switch and keyboard interfacing, 
7 segment LED (embedded C programming). 
9 
3

Introduction to Embedded Systems: Definition, Features, Simple Example 
of Embedded Systems,Applications of embedded systems-Consumer 
9 

 
 
electronics, Robotics, Automobiles 
Embedded System Architecture: HW - Processor, Controller, SoC, 
Memory, Peripherals; SW - Application, Middleware, OS, Device Drivers, 
Tool chain- Assembler, Interpreter, Compiler, Linker, Loader, Debugger 
Embedded system design process: Requirement Analysis, Specification 
Development, HW & SW 
Co-Design and Development, Module Integration, Testing. 
4

Interface 
Programming: Arduino IDE, Sample Code (LED, Switch, DC motor, 
Stepper motor control), Temperature monitoring system using LM35 
Temperature sensor & Seven Segment display 
Embedded Operating system basic concepts: Functional layers in a 
computer system OS terminology, Kernel Functions (Overview only), Types 
of Kernels (Monolithic kernel & Microkernel), Tasks/ Processes.

SEMESTER S7 
INTRODUCTION TO ROBOTICS 
 
Course Code 
OECPT722 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3: 0: 0: 0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
- 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1.  To understand the basic concepts and components of robotic systems. 
2.  To learn principles of robot kinematics, dynamics, and control. 
3.  To gain practical experience with robot programming and sensor integration. 
4.  To explore various applications of robotics in industry and research. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of Robotics :
Introduction to Robotics - Overview of robotics and its applications - 
Historical development and current trends - Basic components and 
classifications of robots 
Robot Anatomy and Components - Sensors: types, functions, and 
integration - Actuators: motors, servos, and their control - Control 
systems and feedback mechanisms 
Robot Kinematics - Coordinate systems and transformations - Forward 
and inverse kinematics 
Robot Dynamics - Introduction to dynamic modeling: Newton-Euler 
and Lagrangian methods 
9 

 
 
2 
Control Systems and Programming : 
Control Systems Fundamentals - Control theory basics: PID control, 
state-space models - Implementing control algorithms in robotics 
Programming Robots - Introduction to robot programming languages 
and environments - Basic programming constructs and techniques 
Perception and Sensor Integration - Types of sensors: vision, 
rangefinders, IMUs - Sensor fusion and data interpretation 
9 
3 
Motion Planning and System Integration : 
Motion Planning - Path planning algorithms: A*, RRT, PRM - 
Motion planning in dynamic environments 
Robotic Systems Integration - Integration of hardware and software 
components - Communication protocols and data exchange 
Robotics in Industry - Applications in manufacturing, healthcare, and 
other fields - Case studies and industry guest speakers - Current 
trends and future directions in robotics 
9 
4 
Advanced Concepts in Robotics : 
Human-robot interaction: Techniques and applications - Autonomous 
robots: Navigation and decision-making - Robotics and AI: 
Integration and future trends 
Emerging Technologies - Soft robotics and bio-inspired robots 
Collaborative robots (cobots) and their applications - Swarm robotics 
and collective behavior 
9

SEMESTER S7 
FUNDAMENTALS OF CYBER PHYSICAL SYSTEMS 
 
Course Code 
OECPT723 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3: 0: 0: 0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
- 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the characteristics, requirements, and architecture of cyber physical systems. 
2. To grasp the fundamentals of microprocessor and microcontroller architecture, focusing on 
Digital Signal Processors. 
3. To master the core principles and mathematical foundations of dynamical systems. 
4. To comprehend cyber-physical system software, emphasizing real-time operating systems and 
job scheduling. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Cyber-Physical Systems: Cyber-Physical Systems (CPS) 
in the real world, Basic principles of design and validation of CPS, Industry 
4.0 AutoSAR, IIOT implications, Building Automation, Medical CPS.  
9 
2 
Platform Components for Cyber Physical Systems: CPS HW platforms - 
Processors, Sensors, Actuators, CPS Network - WirelessHart, CAN, 
Automotive Ethernet, Scheduling Real Time CPS tasks: Table-driven and 
Event driven schedulers, Hybrid schedulers 
9 
3 
Principles of Dynamical Systems: Dynamical Systems and Stability, 
Controller Design Techniques, Performance under Packet drop and Noise 
9 
4 
CPS implementation issues: From features to automotive software 
components, Mapping software components to ECUs 
CPS Performance Analysis: Effect of scheduling, bus latency, sense and 
actuation faults on control performance, network congestion, Building real-
time networks for CPS.  
9

SEMESTER S7 
ADVANCED HUMAN MACHINE INTERFACES  
Course Code 
OECPT724 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Web Technologies, 
Software Engineering
Course Type 
Open Elective 2 
 
Course Objectives: 
      1. To learn the foundation of human machine interaction.   
      2. To understand the importance of human psychology in designing good interfaces. 
      3. To be aware of mobile interaction design and its usage in day – to – day activities. 
      4. To understand various design technologies to meet user requirements. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
FOUNDATIONS OF HMI: 
The Human: History of User Interface Designing, I/O channels, Hardware, 
Software and Operating environment Reasoning and problem solving . The 
computer: Devices, Memory, processing and networks. Interaction: Models, 
frameworks, Ergonomics, styles, elements, interactivity, Paradigms. 
9 
2 
DESIGN & SOFTWARE PROCESS: 
Mistakes performed while designing a computer system, Human interaction 
with computers, importance of human characteristics human consideration, 
Human interaction speeds .Interactive Design basics, process, scenarios, 
navigation, Iteration and prototyping. HMI in software process: software life 
cycle, usability engineering, 
Prototyping in practice, design rationale. Design rules: principles, standards, 
guidelines, rules. Recognize the goals, Goal directed design process. 
Evaluation Techniques: Universal Design. 
9 

 
 
3 
GRAPHICAL USER INTERFACE: 
The graphical User Interface: Popularity of graphics, the concept of direct 
manipulation, graphical systems, Characteristics. Web user Interface: 
Interface popularity, characteristics. The merging of graphical Business 
systems and the Web. Principles of user interface design 
9 
4 
INTERFACE DESIGN FOR MOBILE DEVICES: 
Mobile Ecosystem: Platforms, Application frameworks: Types of Mobile 
Applications: 
Widgets, 
Applications, 
Games, 
Mobile 
Information 
Architecture, Mobile 2.0, Mobile 
Design: Elements of Mobile Design 
INTERACTION STYLES AND COMMUNICATION: 
Windows: Characteristics, Components, Presentation styles, Types of 
Windows, Management, operations. Text messages: Words, Sentences, 
messages and text words, 
Text for web pages. Icons, Multimedia and colors 
9

Embedded system 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Review of embedded system technology. 
2. To understand Concept of Hardware software tradeoff. 
3. To study Real Time Operating System concept. 
4. To understand the current trends in embedded system. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Typical Embedded System: Core of the Embedded System, Memory, 
Sensors and Actuators, 
Communication Interface, Embedded Firmware, Other System Components. 
Characteristics and Quality Attributes of Embedded Systems. 
9 
2 
Hardware Software Co-Design and Program Modelling: Fundamental Issues 
in Hardware 
Software Co-Design, Computational Models in Embedded Design, 
Introduction to Unified 
Modelling Language, Hardware Software Trade-offs. 
9 
3 
Real-Time Operating System (RTOS) based Embedded System Design: 
Operating System Basics, Types of OS, Tasks, Process and Threads, 
Multiprocessing and 
Multitasking, Task Scheduling, Threads, Processes and Scheduling: Putting 
them altogether, Task Communication, Task Synchronization, Device 
Drivers, How to Choose an RTOS. 
9 

 
 
4 
The Embedded System Development Environment: The Integrated 
Development Environment 
(IDE), Types of Files Generated on Cross-compilation, Disassembler / 
Decompiler, Simulators, 
Trends in the Embedded Industry: Processor Trends in Embedded System, 
Embedded OS Trends, Development Language Trends, Open Standards, 
Frameworks and Alliances, Bottlenecks. 
9

SEMESTER S8 
ADVANCED NETWORKED CONTROL APPLICATIONS 
Course Code 
PECPT862 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3: 0: 0: 0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide students with a thorough understanding of the basic principles and concepts of 
networked control systems (NCS). 
2. To develop the ability to model, analyze, and design networked control systems, including 
switched feedback control and boundary control for damped wave equations. 
3. To teach students how to integrate various components of NCS, including sensors, actuators, 
and communication networks, and address implementation challenges. 
4. To introduce concepts of robust control design, including the synthesis of strictly positive real 
(SPR) transfer functions and ensuring system stability and robustness 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Overview of Networked Control Systems: Introduction- Advantages and 
Applications of Control over Network, Brief History of Research Field of 
NCS, NCS Categories and NCS Components - NCS Components, 
Information Acquisition in a Network, Control of Actuators over a Network, 
Communication, NCS Challenges and Solutions - Integration of Components 
and Distribution of Intelligence 
9 
2 
Overview of Agent-based Control and Management for NCS: 
Introduction, From Electricity to Connectivity: Why Agent-based Control 
and Management for Networked Systems, Hosting Mechanism and System 
Architecture for ABC, Design Principle for Networked Control Systems: 
Local Simple, Remote Complex (LSRC), Modular Construction and 
Learning Algorithms of Neuro-fuzzy Networks for LSRC Implementation, 
Issues in Software, Middleware, and Hardware Platforms, Real-world 
Applications. 
9 

 
 
3 
Switched Feedback Control for Wireless Networked Systems: 
Mathematical Modeling of NCS as a Switched System, Optimal Output 
Feedback Control - Gain Tuning of Output Feedback Parameter, Stability 
Investigation. 
Networked Boundary Control of Damped Wave Equations: A Brief 
Introduction to the Smith Predictor, Boundary Control of Damped Wave 
Equations with Large Delays, Stability and Robustness Analysis, Fractional 
Order Case – Problem Formulation, Robustness of Boundary Stabilization, 
Compensation of Large Delays in Boundary Measurement. 
9 
4 
 Design of Robust Strictly Positive Real Transfer Functions:  Definitions 
and Notation, Some Properties of SPR (WSPR) Regions, Characterization of 
SPR (WSPR) Regions, Robust SPR Synthesis: Intersection of WSPR 
Regions, Applications to Robust SPR Synthesis for Low-order Systems - 
The Third-order SPR Synthesis, The Fourth-order SPR Synthesis 
9

SEMESTER S8 
ADVANCED CYBERSECURITY STRATEGIES FOR CPS 
Course Code 
PECPT863 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PECPT743/53, 
PECPT633, PECPT 
523, PECPT413 
Course Type
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To Understand and apply advanced cybersecurity concepts and strategies specific to Cyber-
Physical Systems (CPS). 
2. To develop skills to analyze and assess risks and vulnerabilities in CPS environments. 
3. To Implement and evaluate defense mechanisms and security measures to protect CPS 
effectively. 
4. To Explore and assess emerging trends and technologies in CPS security to address 
contemporary challenges. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Advanced Risk Management Techniques - Advanced risk assessment 
methodologies and frameworks - Integrating risk management into the 
CPS lifecycle 
Advanced Threat Modeling - Detailed threat modeling for sophisticated 
CPS architectures - Tools and techniques for dynamic threat modeling 
Integrative Security Strategies - Combining risk management and threat 
modeling strategies - Developing a cohesive security strategy for 
complex CPS environments 
9 

 
 
2 
Advanced Intrusion Detection Systems - In-depth IDS technologies and 
architectures for CPS - Machine learning and AI in IDS for CPS - 
Configuring and evaluating advanced IDS systems 
Intrusion Prevention and Mitigation Strategies - Advanced intrusion 
prevention techniques - Real-time threat mitigation and response - 
Effective intrusion prevention in high-stakes CPS environments 
9 
3 
Integration and Performance Evaluation - Integrating IDS and IPS into 
CPS - Performance evaluation and tuning of IDS/IPS systems - Best 
practices for IDS/IPS integration and performance optimization 
Secure Firmware and Software Update Mechanisms - Advanced 
techniques for secure firmware updates - Strategies for ensuring update 
integrity and authenticity - Implementing secure update mechanisms in 
CPS 
9 
4 
Vulnerability Assessment and Management - Tools and techniques for 
assessing vulnerabilities in CPS - Managing and mitigating discovered 
vulnerabilities - Conducting vulnerability assessments and applying 
remediation strategies 
Incident Response for Firmware and Vulnerabilities - Incident response 
strategies specific to firmware and vulnerability issues - Forensic 
techniques for firmware-related incidents - Incident response and forensic 
analysis for firmware vulnerabilities. 
Emerging Trends and Technologies - Latest advancements in CPS 
security technologies - Impact of emerging technologies such as quantum 
computing and blockchain on CPS security 
9
