SEMESTER S8 
ADVANCED INTERACTION TECHNIQUES AND USER 
RESEARCH 
Course Code 
PECPT864 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L:T:P:R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
_ 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To Understand the principles of user-centered design and the challenges associated with input 
and interaction techniques. 
2. To Explore the concept of Tangible User Interfaces (TUIs), focusing on the use of physical 
objects as input/output devices. 
3. To learn spatial interactions in Augmented Reality (AR) and Virtual Reality (VR) 
environments to enhance immersion in gaming experiences. 
4. To Investigate and design inclusive mobile user interfaces, considering common UI patterns, 
navigation, gestures, and accessibility for users with disabilities. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Historical Development of Major Advances in HCI: evolution of Human-
Computer Interaction (HCI) from early interfaces (such as command-line 
interfaces) 
to 
modern 
graphical 
user 
interfaces 
(GUIs).Recent 
Developments and Challenges in Input and Interaction Techniques: 
Emerging input methods (touch, gesture, voice, etc.) and their impact on user 
experience, challenges related to designing intuitive and efficient interaction 
techniques. 
9 
2 
Tangible and Embodied User Interactions: tangible interfaces (physical 
objects as input/output devices) and their applications. Embodied 
interactions that consider the user’s body and movement. Mobile 
Interactions: Mobile HCI, including design principles for small screens, 
touch-based interactions, and mobile app usability, challenges specific to 
mobile devices. 
9 

 
 
3 
Augmented and Virtual Reality (AR/VR):AR and VR interfaces, 
including spatial interactions, 3D visualization, and user experience design, 
challenges related to AR/VR hardware and software.Game User Interfaces: 
Game UI/UX design, including HUDs (heads-up displays), menus, controls 
and feedback mechanisms, player engagement and immersion. 
9 
4 
Mobile Interaction Patterns: Common mobile UI patterns (e.g., 
navigation, gestures, touch targets), challenges specific to mobile devices.  
Interaction Techniques for Special User Groups: Investigate designing 
inclusive interfaces for users with disabilities (e.g., visual impairments, 
motor limitations). 
9

Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamental principles of systems engineering  
2. To learn methodologies for designing and integrating complex systems. 
3. To explore the challenges and solutions in CPS engineering. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1

Analysis and Allocation, System Architecture and Design 
System Modeling and Simulation: Introduction to System Modeling, Tools 
and Techniques for Modeling 
9 
2 
System Integration Concepts :Definition and Importance of Integration,

Challenges in System Integration: Interoperability Issues, Managing 
Complexity, Risk Management in Integration 
9 
3

and Privacy ,Scalability and Performance

Course Assessment Method 
 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance
Internal Ex 
Evaluate
Analyse
Total
5
15
10
10
40
 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
Students should evaluate and analyze a real-world problem, assess the proposed solutions, 
conclude which solution is most appropriate for the problem, and then implement the chosen 
solution using executable code or simulate it using relevant software or supported hardware 
platforms. 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Clearly defines the real-world problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors (constraints, resources, 
objectives). 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 4 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
b. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with evidence and logical 
reasoning. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
b. Compares trade-offs, advantages, and disadvantages. 
c. Considers feasibility, scalability, and practical implications. 
4. Implementation (K5 - 4 points) 
a. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions. 
b. Successfully translates the chosen solution into an executable code or 
simulation using relevant software suit or supported hardware platform. 
c. Demonstrates proficiency in simulation / emulation practices (readability, 
efficiency, error handling). 

 
 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem. (K4) 
b. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5) 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, clear implementation, and depth of 
understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S8 
KINEMATICS AND DYNAMICS OF ROBOT  
Course Code 
OECPT822 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
_ 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamentals of robot kinematics and dynamics. 
2. To understand the robot kinematics with velocity and force domain. 
3. To understand the trajectory planning of robot manipulators. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
ROBOT KINEMATICS  
Representing Position and orientation – Homogeneous matrices – Denavit 
Hardenberg representation - Describing a Robot Arm - Forward Kinematics - 
Inverse Kinematics, Case studies on describing the real life robot 
manipulators using D-H representation. 
9 
2 
VELOCITY AND FORCE RELATIONSHIPS  
Velocities in manipulators, Forward and inverse velocity kinematics - 
Manipulator Jacobian and Transforming Velocities between Coordinate 
Frames - Static forces in manipulators - Jacobians in the force domain - 
Cartesian transformation of velocities and static forces. 
9 
3 
ROBOT DYNAMICS  
Acceleration of a rigid body - Equations of Motion – Forward and inverse 
dynamics - Iterative Newton-Euler dynamic formulation – Closed form 
dynamic equations – Lagrangian formulation of manipulator dynamics – 
Formulating manipulator dynamics in Cartesian coordinates. 
9 

 
 
4 
TRAJECTORY PLANNING  
Joint space schemes – Cartesian space schemes – Path generation in run time 
– Description of paths in a robot programming language – Planning path 
when using the dynamic model – Collision-free path planning. 
9

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

Course Code

Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To identify and Analyze Security Threats and Privacy Concerns 
2. To apply Techniques for Securing Data and Ensuring Privacy 
3. To evaluate and Implement Security Measures 
4. To understand and Utilize Emerging Technologies 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Privacy in CPS - Privacy principles and concerns - Data collection, 
handling, and storage in CPS - Privacy regulations 
Data Protection Techniques - Data encryption and decryption methods - 
Authentication and authorization mechanisms - Access control models 
Security Fundamentals for CPS - Basic concepts of cybersecurity - 
Threats and vulnerabilities specific to CPS - Security goals: 
confidentiality, integrity, availability 
9 
2 
Secure Communication in CPS - Secure communication protocols - 
Cryptographic algorithms and key management - Wireless and network 
security considerations 
Integrity and Availability in CPS - Techniques for ensuring data integrity 
- Fault tolerance and redundancy - Protection against denial of service 
attacks 
Threat Modeling and Risk Assessment - Identifying and assessing risks in 
CPS - Threat modeling techniques - Risk mitigation and management 
strategies 
9 

 
 
3 
Safety and Security Integration - Safety-critical systems and their security 
implications - Techniques for integrating safety and security 
Emerging Technologies and Security Implications - Impact of AI and 
machine learning on CPS security - Blockchain and decentralized 
security models - Challenges related to IoT and edge computing 
Security Standards and Compliance - Overview of security standards - 
Compliance requirements and best practices - Implementing and auditing 
security policies 
9 
4 
Practical Applications and Case Studies - Analysis of real-world CPS 
security incidents - Hands-on projects and simulations - Group 
presentations on case studies 
Emerging Threats and Countermeasures - Recent trends in CPS threats 
and attacks - Advanced countermeasures and defense techniques - 
Adapting security strategies to evolving threats 
Future Trends and Innovations - Future directions in CPS security and 
privacy - Role of emerging technologies in shaping the future - 
Predictions and challenges for next-generation CPS 
9

SEMESTER S8 
AUGMENTED AND VIRTUAL REALITY FOR CPS 
 
Course Code 
OECPT824 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L:T:P:R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the fundamental concepts and components of Virtual Reality (VR) systems. 
2. To explain the principles of digital entertainment and development tools in VR, along with 
hardware and software components in AR/VR systems. 
3. To analyze the benefits and challenges of using AR/VR in Cyber-Physical Systems (CPS) 
applications. 
4. To identify and evaluate potential security threats and vulnerabilities in AR/VR CPS 
applications. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Virtual Reality (VR): Fundamental concepts and 
components of VR. Input and output interfaces in VR: trackers, sensors, 
digital gloves, movement capture, video-based input, and 3D menus. Visual, 
auditory, and haptic output devices. AR/VR in CPS: Overview of AR/VR 
technologies, Definition and characteristics of CPS, Applications of AR/VR 
in CPS. 
9 

 
 
2 
Interactive Techniques in VR: Body tracking, hand gestures, and 3D 
manipulation, Development tools and frameworks for VR. Application of 
VR in Digital Entertainment: VR technology in film and TV production. 
Physical exercises and games using VR. Demonstrations of digital 
entertainment through VR.  
AR/VR Fundamentals: AR/VR hardware and software components, Types 
of AR/VR (Marker-based, Markerless, Immersive, Non-Immersive),AR/VR 
development tools and platforms. 
9 
3 
Augmented and Mixed Reality: Taxonomy and features of augmented 
reality (AR).Differences between AR and VR. Challenges in AR systems, 
Visualization techniques for AR. Enhancing interactivity in AR 
environments. 
CPS Components and Architecture: Introduction to CPS components 
(sensors, actuators, control systems), CPS architecture and design principles, 
Integration of AR/VR with CPS components. 
9 
4 
AR/VR Applications in CPS: Industrial automation and control, Healthcare 
and medical systems, Smart homes and buildings, Transportation systems.  
Security and Privacy in AR/VR CPS: Security threats and vulnerabilities 
in AR/VR CPS, Privacy concerns and data protection, Secure design and 
development practices.

Course Outcomes (COs) 
At the end of the course students should be able to:  
Course Outcome 
Bloom’s 
Knowledge Level 
(KL) 
CO1 
Understand the fundamental concepts and components of Virtual 
Reality (VR) and describe the components of a VR system. 
K2 
CO2 
Explain the principles of digital entertainment in VR, the role of 
development tools and frameworks in VR development., hardware and 
software components in AR/VR systems. 
K2 
CO3 
Explain the role of sensors, actuators, and control systems in CPS, 
Identify and describe the components of CPS. 
K2 
CO4 
Illustrate the benefits and challenges of using AR/VR in CPS 
applications and the effectiveness of AR/VR solutions in CPS 
applications. 
K2 
CO5 
Identify and explain potential security threats and vulnerabilities in 
AR/VR CPS and Evaluate the risks associated with these threats and 
vulnerabilities. 
K2 
Note: K1- Remember, K2- Understand, K3- Apply, K4- Analyse, K5- Evaluate, K6- Create
